                                    <div class="top10-vendor-list-item-content top10-content"><p><b>FastComets use case is simple  if you want to reach audiences in Asia without paying a premium, its one of your best and most reliable options. </b><span style="font-weight: 400;">You also wont have to risk it with a local host, where bureaucracy and the language barrier are bound to be an issue.                                     <div class="top10-vendor-list-item-content top10-content"><p>SiteGround has quite an interesting story. Up until lately, it was simply a very good and very dependable cPanel-based provider, meaning it did pretty much what every other shared host does, although usually better. After the hosting industry shakeup caused by cPanel raising its license fees, SiteGround became a different beast altogether.</p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">After months of intense testing and development, SiteGround launched Site Tools, a ridiculously easy-to-use control panel. It lets you set up all important aspects of your hosting quickly, even if youre a total novice.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Butserver performance could do with an improvement. In our testing, page loading speed was consistently slower than the average. Not by much, but its worth noting. Still, </span><b>SiteGround offers an attractive set of features that make it one of the easiest platforms to work with. </b></p>

                                    <div class="top10-vendor-list-item-content top10-content"><p><strong>HostArmada is a fairly new host, but it has managed to catch up to, and in some cases surpass, its older competition.</strong><span style="font-weight: 400;"> It&#8217;s done so by offering great features such as strong security measures across all its plans and a 45-day money-back guarantee. And it&#8217;s turned in some really impressive performance scores.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Our testing showed that HostArmada returned great speeds for both time to first byte (TTFB) and fully loaded. </span><strong>The host fully loaded our test site, on average, in 1.1 seconds.</strong><span style="font-weight: 400;"> Notice that&#8217;s an average score, which means there were often shorter, faster loading speeds.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Speed doesn&#8217;t count for much, though, if your server is constantly down. Fortunately, that&#8217;s not the case with HostArmada. </span><strong>It promises a 99.9% uptime guarantee, and our test site surpassed this mark with a 99.98% uptime score.</strong><span style="font-weight: 400;"> HostArmada also offers credits for downtime due to server maintenance, whether scheduled or incidental. All in all, not bad for a newbie on the hosting scene.</span></p>

                    <div class="top10-row top10-content">                        <div class="top10-section-descBlock"><h2 id="hselect-1"><strong>Popular Hosts That Didnt Make the Cut</strong></h2>
<p></p> Some big names that youve probably encountered in your online travels are missing from my top ten list. While some of them actually have a place in the Worst 10 Hosts list Ill get around to writing one day, others were simply not good enough. 
<p></p> <strong>A2 Hosting &#8211; A2 Hosting is a great shared hosting provider</strong><span style="font-weight: 400;">. It has some of the fastest loading speeds available for a budget host, and its &#8220;anytime&#8221; refund policy makes it easy to see if it&#8217;s a good fit for your site. Unfortunately, on a Top 10 list, there isn&#8217;t room for a deserving #11.</span> 
<p></p> <b>ScalaHosting</b> &#8211; ScalaHosting is another great hosting provider, but we prefer its VPS plans over its shared web hosting. <strong>ScalaHosting makes an ideal &#8220;next step&#8221; </strong>when your site outgrows its shared hosting provider and needs to upgrade to a VPS host. For this reason, we consider ScalaHosting to have more niche appeal, though its still a great choice for new VPS users thanks to its beginner-friendly setup. 
<p></p> <b>Kamatera </b>&#8211; While we like ScalaHosting for the newbie who needs to upgrade, <strong>Kamatera is our top choice</strong>for the advanced or experienced site owner. So why didnt it make the top 10? Kamatera&#8217;s VPS hosting is some of the best around, but it&#8217;s for the techie crowd. If you&#8217;re just looking to host a basic site, or not that great with your server management skills, Kamatera may be too much to handle. 
<p></p> <b>Namecheap </b>&#8211; Namecheap is one of the best options for buying, selling, and registering domain names. But you may not know that <strong>NameCheap is also a fairly decent shared hosting provider</strong>. Still, its not quite good enough to make our top ten list  but it does make the next-best list. 
<p></p> <b>Bluehost</b>  We tested Bluehosts hosting service and found it to be pretty decent. In fact,<b> Bluehost would make a solid budget host </b><b>for the first-time site owner</b>, as its platform is fairly non-techy and easy to use. Bluehost plans are also generously discounted for your first term and very well priced  especially the entry-level options for shared and WordPress hosting. 
<p></p> <strong>GoDaddy</strong>  Its the most famous web host of all time, but who cares? <strong>I signed up to see if it has a place on this list, and when I tested it for three months, what I discovered was a weak service</strong> offered at prices that will get you a better service. 
<p></p> <strong>HostPapa</strong>  I&#8217;ve actually liked HostPapa in the past, and found it to be a generally dependable host. <strong>I signed up againto check how its doing today, and despite the fact that nothing was horrendous, nothing was very good either.</strong> Speeds were disappointing, features were missing, and it offers poor value for money compared to the competition. 
<h2 id="hselect-2">The<strong> Global Web Host Comparison Project: How We Did It</strong></h2>
<p></p> Now, I <em>try</em> to be trusting. When people tell me they can do something, I want to believe them. But when each and every host in existence claims to be the very best, how can anybody take their word for it? 
<p></p> Some hosting providers use the term &#8220;blazing speeds&#8221; loosely, but in reality, it often translates to a slow loading time of three seconds for a basic landing page. Similarly, claiming to offer &#8220;24/7 expert support service&#8221; can be misleading, as the support staff is occasionally available and may not be experts in their field. 
<p></p> The only way to really size these companies up is to test them. And so, I set out on a journey to find the answer to the most important question: 
<p></p> <strong>Which web hosting services are actually the best ones today?</strong> 
<p></p> The process wasnt easy, as the competition was fierce. I broke my analysis down into three smaller questions: 
<ol>
<li>Which are the most popular and most appreciated web hosts today?</li>
<li>What am I looking for in a quality hosting service?</li>
<li>After signing up to and thoroughly testing the contenders, how do they compare in terms of features, performance, ease of use, prices, and support?</li>
</ol> Im happy to report that the project went well, and that I was quite surprised by the results myself. 
<p></p> Before we get started, Ill just mention that we hosted our sites on servers located in these providers US data centers, and you can see the results on this page. But our tests didn&#8217;t end there  <strong>we also had 30+ Website Planet experts from all over the world test these hosts in their own countries, and compare them to local hosts.</strong> To see the results of the local tests, you can change the language in the upper right corner of this page. 
<p></p> Or, simply <a href="#final-010" onclick="trackClickout('event', 'clickin', 'anchorLink', 'final010', this,  );">jump ahead to a summary of results</a> for each host, with coupon discounts. 
<h2 id="hselect-3"><strong>Who Are the Top Web Hosts Available Today?</strong></h2>
<p></p> <strong>To find my contenders for the coveted spot of the worlds #1 host, I looked for versatile companies that offer hosting for the widest range of clients</strong>  from simple shared hosting and managed WordPress to cloud instances, VPS machines, and dedicated servers. 
<p></p> First on the list was the obvious Hostinger. Its a host that just keeps on growing, with many millions of customers. Personally, I didnt think this industry giant would score highly, as oftentimes big companies cruise along on name recognition alone, forgetting about trying to be the best. Still, real testing had to be done to determine this. 
<p></p> I had to delve deeper to find my other hosts, as I didnt want to choose according to popularity alone. <strong>I convened with our Website Planet experts from all over the world (Zoom meetings!) to get their opinions on the best services available today. I also asked around in various web development communities, groups, forums, and subreddits. </strong>Basically, every place I could think of. 
<p></p> We all discussed our past experiences with dozens of web hosts and debated which ones have been a disappointment, which ones have continuously exceeded our expectations, and which ones were just meh. We also compared feedback from actual clients to understand which providers theyve chosen as the most reliable ones. 
<p></p> <strong>The hosting companies that came up the most often during this research phase make up the bulk of my list.</strong> 
<p></p> Ill explain the testing process and discuss the results in a short moment, but first of all, let me introduce Website Planets final list of contenders. You can click each web hosts name to read a full, honest review. 
<ul>
<li><a href="https://www.websiteplanet.com/web-hosting/hostinger/" target="_blank" >Hostinger &#8211; Full Review</a></li>
<li><a href="https://www.websiteplanet.com/web-hosting/1and1-ionos-hosting/" target="_blank" >IONOS  Full Review</a></li>
<li><a href="https://www.websiteplanet.com/web-hosting/interserver/" target="_blank" >InterServer &#8211; Full Review</a></li>
<li><a href="https://www.websiteplanet.com/web-hosting/nexcess/" target="_blank" >Nexcess &#8211; Full Review</a></li>
<li><a href="https://www.websiteplanet.com/web-hosting/kinsta/" target="_blank" >Kinsta &#8211; Full Review</a></li>
<li><a href="https://www.websiteplanet.com/web-hosting/fastcomet/" target="_blank" >FastComet &#8211; Full Review</a></li>
<li><a href="https://www.websiteplanet.com/web-hosting/inmotion-hosting/" target="_blank" >InMotion Hosting &#8211; Full Review</a></li>

</ul> Alright! My dream team was ready, and it was time to start. <strong>The next steps were to test each one separately, obsessively gather the results in way too many Google Sheets, and ultimately, compare and rank them.</strong> Or, you can <a href="#final-conclusions-001" onclick="trackClickout('event', 'clickin', 'anchorLink', 'finalconclusions001', this,  );">jump to the conclusion of this article</a> for coupon discounts on all of the above hosting providers. 
<h2 id="hselect-4"><strong>If You Want To Test a Web Host, You Have To Build a Real Website</strong></h2>
<p></p> <strong>It isnt possible to evaluate the quality of a web host without using it for real, and to use it for real, you need to build a website.</strong> WordPress was my obvious go-to platform, but my website still needed to be about something 
<p></p> Which brings us to a dark and rainy February night. I was waiting for the bus when I realized my head was a bit stuffy and my throat a bit sore. I was catching a cold! Then I remembered an article I&#8217;d read about how vitamins and good nutrition could boost your immune system and possibly avoid the dreaded common cold. Out of my misery and regret, I hit upon a brilliant website idea. 
<p></p> I&#8217;m honored and pleased to introduce you to my very own fictional startup, <i>Nutritionistica!</i> 
<figure id="attachment_3238516" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-3238516"class="wp-caption aligncenter"><span class="ll-img-wrapper "  style="padding:61.469933184855% 0 0; max-width: 850px;"><noscript><img src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2024/01/-web-hosting-category-page-2.jpeg"  width="1347" height="828" alt="Test site home page" /></noscript><img data-src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2024/01/-web-hosting-category-page-2.jpeg"   width="1347" height="828" alt="Test site home page" class="border wp-image-3238516 size-full ll-img"/></span><figcaption id="caption-attachment-3238516"class="wp-caption-text">Nutritionistica isnt a real website, but it IS a great testing page</figcaption></figure> Armed with my revolutionary idea, <b>I bought a flexible WordPress theme, and designed a series of similar websites that I launched on each of the 10 hosts platforms.</b> 
<p></p> For each host, I repeated the same process: 
<p></p> <strong>Before signup, I had a long chat with support to size them up. I played dumb (really dumb), asked a ton of questions, and noted how honest and professional the agents were.</strong> 
<p></p> If they tried to push me into buying an advanced plan I didnt need, told tall tales of how performance in Australia would be amazing (even though their servers are located in the US), or showed a general lack of comprehension, I took points off. 
<p></p> <strong>After that, I created hosting accounts and linked domain names with each of these providers. </strong>I almost always went for the most basic shared hosting plan available, and thoroughly documented the process. I wanted to understand how easy each host is to use, and to check which ones try to weasel some extra bucks off you when youre not looking. I made note of the data center locations, and if the host offered domain name registration, I used it for that, too. 
<p></p> In each instance, I installed WordPress, an SSL certificate, uploaded my custom theme, and evaluated what the plans actually include. What resources will you be getting and what tools are at your disposal? What features are freely available and what lies locked behind a paywall? 
<p></p> When all my websites were up and running, I contacted support again, telling the agents that my loading speed was disappointing, and requested help to make my website load faster. I then proceeded with any suggested optimizations. 
<p></p> <strong>The final step (that is still ongoing) was my performance tests. I measured loading times in the US and all over the world, and enabled uptime monitors to see which hosts were the most reliable. </strong>The tools I used were: 
<ul>
<li>GTmetrix PRO</li>
<li>Sucuri Load Time Tester</li>
<li>UptimeRobots Pro plan</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="hselect-5"><strong>Results and Analysis: How Did Each Host Fare?</strong></h2>
<p></p> After months of experimenting with the hosts and gathering data, I was finally able to complete my mission  <strong>to compare all these hosting providers and find the best one</strong>. 
<p></p> Ive ranked each service in five categories: 
<ol>
<li>Features</li>
<li>Ease of Use</li>
<li>Performance</li>
<li>Support</li>
<li>Pricing</li>
</ol> Youll find a detailed table for each category, followed by an explanation and in-depth discussion of all comparison criteria.

<div class="hightlight-paragraph hightlight-paragraph-transparent" style="text-align: center;"><strong><a href="#final-002" onclick="trackClickout('event', 'clickin', 'anchorLink', 'final002', this,  );">See Coupons for All These Hosts</a></strong></div>
<h3><strong>Disk space</strong></h3>
<p></p> Everything you host is going to take up space. From your WordPress (or any other platform) installation to your text, images, videos, and files, it all counts towards your allotted disk space. <b>InterServer and InMotion Hosting provide unlimited space.</b> 
<p></p> IONOS, Kinsta, GreenGeeks, and SiteGround provide the smallest amount of space, with Nexcess, FastComet, HostArmada, and Hostinger doing slightly better. 
<p></p> Still, dont jump to the conclusion that more is always better. 10GB is certainly enough for blogs, business pages, and even e-commerce stores with thousands of HD pics. <strong>Unlimited space sounds amazing, but its always bound to some fair use agreement</strong> and youre never the one who gets to decide whats fair. 
<h3><strong>Bandwidth or data transfer</strong></h3>
<p></p> When people visit your website, the host sends them the page they requested. In the same way that all your hosted data counts towards your disk space limit, your bandwidth is how much data youre allowed to send in a month. <strong>The more visitors you have, the more bandwidth youll require.</strong> 
<p></p> <strong>SiteGround and Kinsta provide the least amount, although they will still do well for small-to-medium audiences. </strong>Most of the other hosts do significantly better, offering unlimited bandwidth. However, much like with disk space, these unlimited claims are often misleading. Youll likely encounter restrictions if your site uses too many resources. For this reason, <b>Nexcess is the true bandwidth champion</b>, guaranteeing an obscene amount of traffic. 
<h3><strong>Control panel</strong></h3>
<p></p> Do you speak Linux? Nope. Thats why control panels were invented. They allow you to easily edit and configure your hosting solution, from DNS records to databases and email accounts. 
<p></p> <b>Most hosts offer cPanel, which is the most popular option out there. </b>As far as basic hosting management is concerned, you can never go wrong with it. Hostinger, IONOS, and SiteGround developed panels of their own, and while all of them mimic cPanel in some ways, they fail to deliver an equally powerful solution. 
<p></p> <strong><strong>Kinsta</strong> and Nexcess</strong><strong>completely did away with the idea of a fully-fledged control panel.</strong> They dont offer nearly as many options as the contenders, but theres a reason for that  <strong>both services are managed, meaning most configuration is already taken care of for you.</strong> 
<h3><strong>Auto-installers</strong></h3>
<p></p> Installing CMSs (content management systems) like WordPress used to be a tedious manual process, but today, most providers offer an easy-to-use automatic installation. 
<p></p> <b>Most hosts went with Softaculous, a very capable auto-installer that offers easy installation for hundreds of CMSs. </b>Hostinger, IONOS, and SiteGround have self-developed solutions that work similarly. <b>Kinsta and Nexcess, true to their promise of managing things for you, dont give you access to such a service. Instead, your CMS of choice comes pre-installed.</b> 
<h3><strong>Platform support</strong></h3>
<p></p> What CMS can you actually install with each service? WordPress is popular, but its far from the only website platform available today  hundreds of options exist, from Joomla and Magento to self-developed PHP-based projects. 
<p></p> <strong>Almost all hosts provide full platform support, meaning that you can run any CMS you desire.</strong> SiteGround is slightly more limited, offering a few dozen options or so. Nexcess supports the most popular platforms, but servers are highly-optimized for each type; or, you can opt for a Flexible Cloud Plan and host whatever you wish. Kinsta is strictly a WordPress service<strong>,</strong> and cant be used for any other CMS. 
<h3><strong>SSL certificates</strong></h3>
<p></p> <strong>I cant stress the importance of an SSL certificate enough. </strong>It secures and encrypts your visitors data, guaranteeing their safety if they are logging in to or submitting data on your site. Its a <em>must</em> for e-commerce sites, and is also known to positively affect Google rankings and SEO in general. 
<p></p> While SSL certificates used to be quite expensive, today theres a much cheaper solution. <strong>Lets Encrypt SSL certificates are free to use, and any host can easily choose to provide them. That is exactly what almost all of these hosts have done.</strong> 
<h3><strong>SSL Qualys score</strong></h3>
<p></p> <strong>Qualys tests the strength of your websites SSL protection,</strong> ranking it on an A to F scale. Care about your visitors, your SEO, and about being a responsible adult? Anything less than an A ranking is cause for concern. 
<p></p> <strong>Apart from FastComet and InMotion Hosting, all other hosts scored an A or above, </strong>guaranteeing you complete peace of mind. What should you make of the B score? That these hosts couldve done better, but for reasons unknown, chose to neglect this aspect of the service. Thats bad news. 
<h3><strong>Backups</strong></h3>
<p></p> While all auto-installers can be configured to run a CMS backup onto your disk space, <strong>Im looking for full system backups that are automatically made and stored on a remote server.</strong> So if your hosting space was compromised by hackers, an untouched backup still exists. 
<p></p> <strong>Most hosts only provide these backups as a paid add-on, which is a crying shame.</strong> Its absolutely necessary. InterServer doesnt provide such a service at all for its shared plans. GreenGeeks performs nightly backups that are available in the event of a service malfunction, but you cant access them yourself. 
<p></p> <strong>The only saints are IONOS</strong><strong>, Nexcess</strong><strong>, Kinsta and SiteGround</strong><strong>.</strong> They provide you with easy access to backups, and let you freely restore them. You can also run more backups on demand. 
<h3><strong>Number of domains</strong></h3>
<p></p> This does not refer to the domain names you&#8217;ve registered, but to the number of separate websites you can host with your plan. One domain is obviously the minimum, and is usually what basic plans offer. Pay more for advanced plans, get more domains. 
<p></p> This is true of all the hosts on this list except InMotion Hosting and InterServer. InMotion Hosting gives you 2 domains on the basic plan<strong>, while InterServers plan comes with unlimited domains</strong><strong> which is undoubtedly the hosts biggest selling point.</strong> Just remember that behind-the-scenes computing resources are still limited, so use this plan for running multiple landing page sites and average-sized blogs  not resource-hungry megastores. 
<h3><strong>Number of email accounts</strong></h3>
<p></p> If you want a domain-specific email account, and are planning to use this address for business purposes, be sure to check what your host offers. <b>Hostinger and IONOS, for example, offer just a single email account with their basic plans. GreenGeeks does better, with 50</b><b>. </b>All others, except Kinsta, let you open unlimited accounts. 
<p></p> <strong>Kinsta, sadly, has no email hosting <em>at all</em>,</strong> meaning youll have to shell out for a separate email service such as G Suite. 
<h3><strong>CDN</strong></h3>
<p></p> Your website is hosted on a physical server <em>somewhere</em> in the world. The farther your visitors are from this location, the longer it will take them to load your website. Looking to offset this? Enter a CDN (content delivery network). A CDN caches (creates copies) of your website&#8217;s assets (images, code, and rendered versions of your site&#8217;s pages) and spreads them over a global network of servers, speeding up content delivery. 
<p></p> <strong>Nexcess and Kinsta excel here, giving you access to premium CDN services. Most other hosts offer easy, one-click integration with the 3rd-party Cloudflare.</strong> Cloudflare has a free service, but its not the fastest. Hostinger hides this easy integration behind a paywall, which is truly ridiculous. 
<h3><strong>Caching</strong></h3>
<p></p> A CDN isnt the only thing that can cache your website pages. Your hosting server can do it too! Why let your server rebuild your homepage every time a visitor arrives, when its the exact same homepage every time? A caching tool creates ready-to-send versions of your pages, significantly reducing the load on your server. 
<p></p> <strong>Almost all of these hosts offer some form of server-level caching, </strong>which allows site pages to be delivered more promptly.<strong> Sadly, A2 Hosting and InMotion offer no such option,</strong> limiting you to the vastly inferior client-level caching plugins. FastComet only includes caching in its advanced plans. 
<h3><strong>Security tools</strong></h3>
<p></p> A malware scanner, WAF (web application firewall), and any other tool that helps you secure your hosting, are highly recommended. Its a dangerous world online, and its better to be safe than sorry. 
<p></p> Most hosts turned out to be disappointing on this front, not providing a single security tool out of the box. Among the ones that do, its usually a basic cPanel malware scanner. InterServer takes the prize here by letting you access a full range of scanners and security suites<strong>, all pre-installed and easy to use.</strong> 
<div class="hightlight-paragraph hightlight-paragraph-purple">
<h3><strong>Features  Bottom Line</strong></h3>
<p></p> <strong>InterServer and Nexcess share the win.</strong> InterServer wins by using cPanel, going the unlimited route, and including powerful security measures. Nexcess and its custom panel might not have as many security tools, but the inclusion of automatic 30-day backups generated a lot of appreciation on my side.

<h2 id="hselect-7" class=""><strong>Ease of Use</strong></h2>
<p></p> Not enough companies take the time to plan out the user experience and make it as seamless as possible. Still, ease of use is of the utmost importance. Learning how to play nice with a badly designed service can cost you hours, even days.

<p></p> <strong><a href="#final-003" onclick="trackClickout('event', 'clickin', 'anchorLink', 'final003', this,  );">Get Coupon Deals for All These Hosts</a></strong> 
</div>
<h3><strong>Easy signup</strong></h3>
<p></p> Nobody wants signing up to a service to feel like high school homework. Ive ranked each service on a 1-5 scale according to how easy it was to get on board, which in a perfect world consists of me inputting my email address, choosing a password, and entering payment information. If they asked me annoying questions, requested irrelevant data, or in any way complicated this process  I took points off. 
<p></p> Most hosts did pretty well here. Some had me going through extra pages and were slightly confusing, but thats a relatively minor offense. Still, Nexcess<strong>and <strong>Kinsta</strong> </strong><strong>asked for the least amount of details, did not hinder my progress in any way, and basically let me finish the whole process in under a minute.</strong> 
<h3><strong>Immediate account activation</strong></h3>
<p></p> Silly me, thinking that after signing up and entering my very legitimate payment information, Id immediately be activated. How wrong I was. Many hosts have anti-fraud protocols in place, and these protocols were very quick to block my purchase and send me back to the drawing board. You might not get tagged by the protocols, but in many cases, I was. 
<p></p> <strong>Hostinger, IONOS, Kinsta</strong><strong>, and InMotion Hosting</strong><strong>were the only hosts to immediately activate me.</strong> SiteGround and InterServer made small charges to my credit card, which took a while to show up. I then had to confirm these to be verified successfully. FastComet asked for a screenshot of my credit card charge. 
<p></p> <strong><b>GreenGeeks </b>blocked my order on account of fraud.</strong> The process of getting in touch with the sales team, providing a copy of my passport (which I didnt feel comfortable <em>at all</em> with), and finally switching to PayPal, took two days. 
<h3><strong>Connecting the domain</strong></h3>
<p></p> Ranked on a 1-5 scale. Its <em>really</em> easy to score highly here. All a host has to do is to put the nameservers or server IP in a visible spot, and include a quick guide on what to do. How can you fail this super-basic step that every client has to go through? 
<p></p> <strong>Kinsta made this surprisingly difficult, and had me manually configuring DNS records. This is something that almost all other hosts automatically do for you,</strong> and it took me an hour Im never getting back. With InMotion Hosting, I needed to change my primary domain. It took me time to find out this extra step was required, but the process itself was relatively easy. 
<h3><strong>Installing a CMS</strong></h3>
<p></p> From 1 to 5. As long as an auto-installer is included, this is easy. Just click it, enter your new website details, and go live. 
<p></p> SiteGround and Hostinger did well, letting me install WordPress automatically right after signup.<strong> IONOS, Nexcess, Kinsta, and InMotion Hosting </strong><strong>were the best  </strong>WordPress was already pre-installed and waiting for me on WordPress hosting plans. 
<h3><strong>Using the account area</strong></h3>
<p></p> Ranked from 1 to 5. Between the hosting control panel and you stands the account area. <strong>This is usually some weird twilight zone that lets you view your plans, go over billing, purchase more stuff, or really, sometimes, just <em>be there</em>. </strong>The more complicated it is to navigate, or the more its filled with annoying upsells, the less happy I get. 
<p></p> <strong>InterServer scores very low here as its account area is an under-designed mess,</strong> filled with upsells and links to products you dont have. Hostinger is very sleek, but constant upsell popups pushing you to upgrade your plan or purchase more add-ons are a pain. InMotion Hostings account area looks like it was designed by my grandma, who despite being a phenomenal person, is not a user interface expert. 
<p></p> <strong><strong>Kinsta</strong> and Nexcess</strong><strong>offer what is basically a perfect user experience,</strong> seamlessly integrating an easy-to-use account area with the hosting control panel. That means less time loading pages, navigating menus, or making wild guesses about what lies where. 
<div class="hightlight-paragraph hightlight-paragraph-purple">
<h3><strong>Ease of Use  Bottom Line</strong></h3>
<p></p> <strong>Kinsta and Nexcess, despite suffering from some silly issues that couldve easily been remedied, still win this one.</strong> Pre-installed CMSs and super easy-to-use account areas mean youll be able to enjoy the full power of your hosting while wasting the least amount of time trying to fiddle with it.

Im sad to say that most of them are going about it entirely the wrong way. <a href="https://www.websiteplanet.com/blog/web-hosting-server-performance-tests/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><strong>If youre interested in learning how to do it <em>right</em>, weve written a full article on the subject</strong></a>.

<div class="hightlight-paragraph hightlight-paragraph-transparent" style="text-align: center;"><strong><a href="#final-004" onclick="trackClickout('event', 'clickin', 'anchorLink', 'final004', this,  );">Get Coupon Discounts for All These Hosts</a></strong></div>
<h3><strong>Data center locations</strong></h3>
<p></p> The geographic locations where the companies servers are. Most hosts operate more than one data center, although theres nothing wrong with focusing on just one. Just remember, you need a data center thats close to your target or majority audience. Running a French politics blog, written in French, aimed at French citizens? Dont host it in Los Angeles. Go for Paris, or at least Amsterdam. 
<p></p> <strong>Using Google Cloud&#8217;s servers, Kinsta is easily the winner when trying to reach those hard-to-serve audiences</strong><strong> in such locations as Japan or Australia. FastComet comes in a close second</strong><strong>,</strong> and most other hosts operate from Amsterdam and the US east coast, sometimes also running a data center in Singapore. InMotion Hosting and InterServer also run data centers in Los Angeles, making them a great choice for US west coast audiences. 
<h3><strong>Web server</strong></h3>
<p></p> The technology that powers your website. Think of it as the code (not to be confused with the actual <em>server</em>, which is the physical machine that runs the code) that was written by some very talented people to make sure your visitors can view your pages and interact with your site. Apache and its successor, Apache 2.x, are the oldest web server technologies commonly used today. Theyre great and reliable, but newer web servers, like NGINX and LiteSpeed, are known to outperform Apache. 
<p></p> <strong>IONOS, InMotion Hosting, and FastComet are all lagging behind in this aspect, as they only offer Apache.</strong> 
<h3><strong>Loading speed</strong></h3>
<p></p> Page loading speed, measured in seconds, is based on a large number of factors, some under your control and some beyond it. Visitors from different locations, and sometimes even the same visitor at a different time of the day, will get slightly different loading speeds. Still,<strong> average loading times of over 3 seconds aren&#8217;t desirable </strong>Many users will simply click away if they have to wait too long for a site to load.To help gauge each hosting providers performance.<strong> Ive used GTmetrix to measure loading speeds over a long period of time.</strong> 
<p></p> <strong>GTmetrix speeds</strong>: How long the GTmetrix testing server took to load our website, in seconds. I ran these speed tests on an almost daily basis, and now I present you with the average speed to fully load our test site. Unsurprisingly, our top two hosts, <b>Hostinger</b> and <b>IONOS,</b> returned the fastest scores. 
<h3><strong>Uptime</strong></h3>
<p></p> Uptime is measured in percentage, and I used UptimeRobot to test it over several months. 100% means the website was never down. 99% means that it was down for 1% of the testing period. Thats 1% of the time when no visitor was able to view your website. Translate that to lost customers, lost readers, whatever  they may never try to visit your website again. Most hosts guarantee (or at least aim for) around 99% uptime. I like my websites shaken, not stirred, and with at least 99.99% uptime. 
<p></p> <strong>I&#8217;m happy to report that uptime results were fantastic for all hosts. Give it time  when they falter, Ill be here with the update.</strong> 
<h3><strong>Uptime guarantee</strong></h3>
<p></p> Reliable hosts guarantee uptime in their SLA (Service-Level Agreement). They stand by their guarantee, and offer you reimbursement if they cant live up to their promise. 
<p></p> Thing is, some companies are sneaky. They use misleading language to avoid responsibility, or define an uptime guarantee in ways that work for them  but not for you. 
<p></p> For example, InMotion Hosting advertises a 99.9% guarantee, but this isnt backed up within its Hosting Agreement. So, theyre actually under no formal obligation to provide you with 99.9% uptime. <b>Hostinger guarantees uptime under very vague conditions, and will only reimburse you for 5% of your fee</b> as solely determined by them. I cant count these as actual guarantees. 
<p></p> Even premium host Nexcess isnt entirely truthful. It proudly displays a 100% uptime guarantee, but if you dig into the SLA, youll find that youd need to accumulate 15 minutes of downtime across a given month to be due compensation. This is hardly a 100% guarantee, but at least its still better than the standard 99.9% guarantee. 
<div class="hightlight-paragraph hightlight-paragraph-purple">
<h3><strong>Performance &#8211; Bottom Line</strong></h3>
<p></p> <strong>The winners are clear: Kinsta, Nexcess, and Hostinger.</strong> How the budget-friendly Hostinger manages to be as speedy and reliable as the two most expensive services on this list is beyond me. Hostinger agents did provide me with a long and useful optimization guide, but I never expected performance to be this great.

<p></p> When you have a question, or simply need help, youll have to rely on the hosts support agents, tutorials, and knowledge base. If youre a beginner or a little less tech-savvy, you have to be sure that these guys will be there for you.

<h3><strong>Pre-sales support</strong></h3>
<p></p> Ranked from 1 to 5. If youre looking to sign up, you probably have questions. Thats why having a professional sales support agent available is important. One that knows their stuff and wont try to sell you plans or products you dont need. I tried to talk with all the hosts before signing up. Surprisingly, it wasnt always an option. Live chat is obviously my preferred way, but prompt email responses are also appreciated. Just dont make me call you  I dont want to. 
<p></p> <strong>Nexcess professional agent was honest, quick to respond, and simply got me psyched about signing up. FastComet was also great</strong><strong>, promptly answering my questions with a solid knowledge of the service and no overselling.</strong> A2 Hosting and GreenGeeks faltered here and there, but were generally dependable. Best thing about all of these hosts? They were available through live chat. 
<p></p> <strong>Hostinger made me use email.</strong> I got good answers in less than an hour, but I was still not impressed. Kinsta also made me use email, which was surprising considering how much the service costs. I didnt get an answer to my questions, but the option to make a phone call was available. Ugh. 
<p></p> <b>I had a lot of trouble getting in touch with IONOS sales team. </b>The live chat service was frequently unavailable, and there didnt seem to be an email address for sales support. Again, the only option left to me was phone support  which was a bit of a pain as I only had a few brief questions. 
<p></p> <strong>InterServers agent was disappointing. He had a weak grasp of the English language,</strong> and didnt seem to understand how loading speeds are affected by physical distance from the data center. 
<p></p> SiteGround doesn&#8217;t get a score in this category because the company didn&#8217;t offer any pre-sales support when I tested it. It now offers live chat, so we&#8217;ll update this page once we have a chance to test it. 
<h3><strong>Support channels</strong></h3>
<p></p> As a customer, I want to be able to contact support when I need it, in the way most convenient to me. I also want live chat and the option to get support through phone, email, and tickets. 
<p></p> <strong>All of the hosts offer the standard mix of chat, tickets, and phone support. </strong>Nexcess was particularly quick to respond on live chat and equally quick to offer a solution. 
<h3><strong>In-house support</strong></h3>
<p></p> To provide the most reliable support, the team needs to be in-house. Hopefully, that means in the very same building as the technicians, sales staff, and all other company personnel. <strong>Outsourcing support to second and third-rate manpower companies in India or elsewhere makes things a lot cheaper for the hosts themselves, but it spells disaster for you.</strong> When speaking with such agents, expect broken English, a general lack of knowledge, and sometimes a complete inability to assist outside of reciting scripted responses. 
<p></p> <strong>Eight of the ten did okay, but not A2 Hosting and InterServer.</strong> The situation with InterServer became downright depressing as testing progressed. Agents struggled with basic English, and interactions ended up taking way longer than they should. A2 Hostings outsourced support is not as bad, although you still have to use baby-talk with them, at least for most of the time. 
<h3><strong>Availability</strong></h3>
<p></p> When I contact a support team, I want an agent to be available to me 24/7. And to answer my message in a timely manner, which in my book is around 30 seconds. I gathered data on how long it really took to get support, and what the working hours were. 
<p></p> <b>All hosts advertise a 24/7 support service, but with some, this isnt actually the case. </b>Hostinger, IONOS, and InMotion Hosting took a very long time to answer questions on live chat, sometimes making me wait up to an hour, or even longer. 
<h3><strong>Professionalism</strong></h3>
<p></p> What good is a support agent that answers immediately, but doesnt know the first thing about connecting a domain to a hosting account, or about setting up an SSL certificate? No good. Ive ranked them from 1 to 5 based on my experiences. I had multiple interactions with each providers support team, and got a good idea of the overall standards. 
<p></p> <strong>Simply put, you cant count on InterServer for help via live chat.</strong> The agents are not trained for the job, and are only there to give you the illusion of support. InterServer does have actual agents available through tickets, so I eventually gave up on chat support. 
<p></p> <strong>SiteGround, Nexcess</strong><strong>, Kinsta, and GreenGeeks </strong><strong>are the complete opposite. These guys <em>know</em> hosting.</strong> They have experience with it. They were able to handle every problem I had, quickly and with ease. 
<p></p> What about the rest? Theyre hit or miss. With FastComet, for example, one agent tried to reinstall my website in an attempt to solve an unrelated issue. Another agent turned out to be an optimization machine, spending a long half hour improving my sites loading speeds and earning an A in my book. 
<h3><strong>Going the extra mile</strong></h3>
<p></p> Sometimes youre going to be in need of a helping hand, but the specific issue youre dealing with isnt covered by the service level agreement. Many times, the agents know exactly what needs to be done. Its up to them to either make you a happy customer, or to cling to rules and regulations and say Sorry! Thats not part of the service! Its okay to do the latter. Really. But if you want a place in my heart, youve gotta go the extra mile. 
<p></p> <b>InterServer fails miserably because it can barely go the first mile</b>, never mind the extra ones. Nexcess was open to making my life easier  a Nexcess agent installed a WordPress theme for me. While this is a one-click no-brainer, many other hosts tell you to either Google it or look for the button. FastComet also scored highly here, although it really seems to depend on the given agent, and on how Jupiter aligns with Mars. 
<p></p> <strong>But the absolute winner here? GreenGeeks. </strong>Im not exaggerating  these guys <i>want</i> to help. Badly. They will sit with you for an hour and guide you through how to use WordPress for the first time. They will optimize your website for you, thoughtfully taking care of every issue and providing full information each step of the way. Theyre the best. 
<div class="hightlight-paragraph hightlight-paragraph-purple">
<h3><strong>Support  Bottom Line</strong></h3>
<p></p> <strong>GreenGeeks, knocking it out of the park. As I said, this is how support <em>should</em> be.</strong> Nexcess, FastComet, and Kinsta are good, but they all suffer from some issue  annoying ticket system, minor mistakes, or a strict adherence to not doing anything theyre not obligated to do.

<div class="hightlight-paragraph hightlight-paragraph-transparent" style="text-align: center;"><strong><a href="#final-006" onclick="trackClickout('event', 'clickin', 'anchorLink', 'final006', this,  );">See Coupons for All These Providers</a></strong></div>
<h3>Entry-level monthly plan price</h3>
<p></p> Simply put, the monthly price of the most basic shared hosting plan. Sometimes monthly plans arent available, and in those cases Ive calculated the monthly price as the plan price divided by the number of months. 
<p></p> <strong>Wondered where Kinsta and Nexcess were going to get you? Its right here. The basic monthly price is much, much higher than any other host on this list. Kinsta is actually six times more expensive than InterServer</strong><strong>,</strong> whos the obvious winner. Even when paying monthly, the price is still an amazingly fair $5. 
<h3><strong>Annual term plan price</strong></h3>
<p></p> The trick with most hosting companies is, to get the best possible prices, you need to sign up for the longest possible term. In the table above, I&#8217;ve included the monthly price if you sign up for a year with any host. 
<p></p> <strong>Hostinger becomes one of the absolute cheapest options in the history of web hosting when you sign up for four years.</strong> Its truly an amazing price, but its up to you to consider how your needs will change in four years  the plan will likely stay the same. 
<h3><strong>Payment periods</strong></h3>
<p></p> Some people want to sign up to a service and start a business that you <em>know</em> is going to be around for a long time. You might be alright with signing up for years in advance. But otherswant flexibility. Monthly payments give you the ability to change your mind and be done with the plan by next month. 
<p></p> <strong>Sadly, youre not getting that with InMotion Hosting, where its a minimum one-year signup</strong><strong>. SiteGround is even worse,</strong> letting you choose a monthly trial plan, but after a month, announcing that the trial is over and now its either a yearly subscription or bust. 
<p></p> <b>Interserver offers the most flexible payment periods</b>, with a staggering number of options. You can sign up for 1 month, 3 months, 6 months, or 1-3 years. 
<h3><strong>Payment options</strong></h3>
<p></p> Please God, let me pay with PayPal. But credit cards are also okay. And I appreciate having other options, like bitcoin or chickens. 
<p></p> <strong>Kinsta gave me no PayPal and no chickens, instead sticking to credit cards like its the jolly 1990s</strong>. GreenGeeks let me pay with PayPal, but its not recurring. I had to manually pay my monthly invoice <i>every</i> time. These were both major disappointments. 
<h3><strong>No automatic upsells</strong></h3>
<p></p> When signing up to the service, some hosts automatically add extra services you never asked for. Because they want you to pay more. Its a sneaky, disgusting business practice. 
<p></p> <strong>The main offenders here are SiteGround and InMotion Hosting. They all seem to think that they know better than you, and add a backup service or some other extra</strong> that balloons the monthly cost past the Kinsta stratosphere. I recommend being <em>very</em> careful with them during the signup process. 
<h3><strong>No hidden fees</strong></h3>
<p></p> Hidden fees are almost as annoying as upsells. These are fees that surprisingly pop up, usually when youre already set on buying the product. Made-up terms like a setup fee (its all automatic  nobody is setting up your new account) that come with a $15 price tag are a big no-no in my book. 
<p></p> <strong>SiteGround fails this one completely, and on multiple levels. It charges a setup fee only when signing up for the monthly trial</strong> (what kind of trial costs extra?), and doesnt refund it even if you sign up for an annual plan after the month is over.<strong> <b>GreenGeeks also has a setup fee in place, but a sales agent was kind enough to remove it upon my request.</b></strong> 
<h3><strong>Money-back guarantees</strong></h3>
<p></p> If hosting with a company doesnt work out, youll want to bid them <i>adieu</i> and get your money back. Thankfully, <b>all the hosts on our list have a money-back guarantee or a free trial, allowing you to try them completely risk-free.</b> 
<p></p> Its worth pointing out how<b> InMotion Hosting gives you a full three months</b><b>to make up your mind, which is one of the more generous policies Ive encountered.</b> 
<h3><strong>Free domain name</strong></h3>
<p></p> I dont recommend hosting your website and purchasing your domain name from the same company, but sometimes the deal is too good not to consider. 
<p></p> <strong>IONOS, GreenGeeks,</strong><strong> and InMotion Hosting</strong><strong>will throw in a free domain name if you sign up for a year or longer.</strong> InterServer lets you purchase a heavily discounted one, and Hostinger changes its offering often. I got a free domain name when signing up, but it <em>isnt</em> always there. 
<h3><strong>Domain name registration</strong></h3>
<p></p> Even if you got a free domain, itll only be free for one year. The second year, youll pay full price. <strong>FastComet</strong> and <strong>Hostinger</strong> have the lowest prices among these ten (for a .com domain), and all others are surprisingly expensive. But <strong>seriously, guys, dont buy a domain where you host. Just go with <a href="https://www.websiteplanet.com/web-hosting/namecheap/" target="_blank" ><strong>Namecheap</strong> </a></strong><strong>or </strong><strong>Namesilo</strong><strong>. Theyre cheaper, more reliable, and include WHOIS protection for free</strong>. 
<div class="hightlight-paragraph hightlight-paragraph-purple">
<h3><strong>Pricing  Bottom Line</strong></h3>
<p></p> <strong>This is one section where Kinsta didnt stand a chance.</strong> Our speedy and powerful hero is not only more expensive, but also offers less flexibility and no payment methods other than credit cards. Shame. 
<p></p> <strong>The winners are Hostinger and InterServer. Hostinger easily wins for long-term hosting,</strong> boasting what are simply the cheapest plans on the market. You can sign up for anything between one month and four years, and you can even pay with bitcoin if you so desire. 
<div class="shortcode-external-button-link"><a href="https://www.websiteplanet.com/goto.php?id=46365&lang=en&deep_id=0&deep_name=&btn_name=ButtonExternalUrl_46365_top10_164_690567&post_id=164&pageview_id=0&direct_link=&type=top10&amp=0" data-id="46365" rel="sponsored noopener norefferer" class="clickoutLink shortC" target="_blank" onclick="trackClickout('event', 'clickout', 'ButtonExternalUrl_46365_top10_164_690567', 'hostinger', this,  true  );">See Hostinger&#8217;s Latest Plans &gt;&gt;</a></div>
<p></p> <strong>InterServer is best for keeping things flexible and affordable. The monthly price is <em>very</em> fair,</strong> making InterServer an obvious choice for you savvy customers who want to get more and pay less without committing for years to come. 
<div class="shortcode-external-button-link"><a href="https://www.websiteplanet.com/goto.php?id=251823&lang=en&deep_id=0&deep_name=&btn_name=ButtonExternalUrl_251823_top10_164_690568&post_id=164&pageview_id=0&direct_link=&type=top10&amp=0" data-id="251823" rel="sponsored noopener norefferer" class="clickoutLink shortC" target="_blank" onclick="trackClickout('event', 'clickout', 'ButtonExternalUrl_251823_top10_164_690568', 'interserver', this,  true  );">See InterServer&#8217;s Best Deals &gt;&gt;</a></div>

<h2 id="hselect-11"><div id="final-conclusions-001">Final Conclusions and Recommendations</div></h2>
<p></p> Feeling a bit lost after being bombarded with all this data? Well, not to toot my own horn or anything, but the most detailed hosting comparison ever done <em>can</em> seem confusing at first. 
<p></p> <strong>Before I go into specific use cases for each host, let me reiterate one thing  there are no bad hosts in our Top 10.</strong> There are no mediocre hosts on this list. All ten companies provide a solid, dependable service, and the rankings only have to do with how well they performed relative to each other. 
<p></p> <strong>Now lets see which host is best for <em>you</em>.</strong> 
<h3><strong><a href="https://www.websiteplanet.com/goto.php?id=46365&lang=en&deep_id=0&deep_name=&btn_name=VendorExternalUrl_46365_top10_164_974874&post_id=164&pageview_id=0&direct_link=&type=top10&amp=0"  rel="sponsored noopener norefferer" data-id="46365" class="clickoutLink boldLink shortC" target="_blank" onclick="trackClickout('event', 'clickout', 'VendorExternalUrl_46365_top10_164_974874', 'hostinger', this,  true  );">Hostinger  Best for Personal Websites, Has the Cheapest Long-Term Plans</strong><strong></a></strong></h3>
<p></p> Im going to be completely honest here  if youre running a business-critical website or an e-commerce store thats bound to experience huge traffic spikes, dont choose Hostinger. <strong>This is shared hosting, meaning its best for projects like blogs, portfolios, businesses looking to get an online presence,</strong> and the like. If thats what youre looking for, go for the long-term plan and enjoy some of the cheapest hosting in the world. My testing still has Hostinger out-performing almost all other hosts in terms of speed, and theres plenty to love about the simplified control panel.

<h2 id="hselect-12"><strong>FAQ</strong></h2>
<h3 class="shortcode-faq-question-inline">Can I host a website for free?</h3>
<span class="shortcode-faq-answer-inline">Kind of. Free hosting exists, but while it wont cost you money, it will cost you visitors. Free services are slow, unreliable, and insecure, and if you use one, you should expect anything from frequent downtime to your entire project being hacked and/or blacklisted. Its best to avoid these issues altogether, and <a href="#hostinger">go with a great cost-effective solution like Hostinger instead</a>.</span> 
<h3 class="shortcode-faq-question-inline">Can I change my web hosting company?</h3>
<span class="shortcode-faq-answer-inline">Yes, you can. If youre unhappy with your current web host, know that <a href="#final-008" onclick="trackClickout('event', 'clickin', 'anchorLink', 'final008', this,  );">many of the companies on this list</a> provide free website migrations. Contact support after signing up to your new service, and the agents will happily take care of everything for you. Some hosts, like InterServer, will even clean a hacked website as part of the process.</span> 
<h3 class="shortcode-faq-question-inline">Which web host is best for WordPress?</h3>
<span class="shortcode-faq-answer-inline">While all hosts on this list fully support WordPress, their use cases differ. If youre looking to build a WordPress blog or a simple business website, <a href="#hostinger">Hostinger should definitely be first</a>on your list. <a href="#interserver">InterServer is your best bet</a> for multiple low-resource WordPress installations, whether youre creating landing pages or running a link-building project. For mission-critical websites and WooCommerce stores, go with <a href="#kinsta">Kinsta</a> or <a href="#nexcess">Nexcess</a>.</span> 
<h3 class="shortcode-faq-question-inline">Which web host is best for small businesses?</h3>
<span class="shortcode-faq-answer-inline"><a href="#hostinger">Hostinger is an excellent and affordable option</a> if youre looking to showcase your business, but I wouldnt recommend using it for a full-fledged e-commerce store. If your website is going to be the center of your business strategy, and especially if you plan on selling products, <a href="#nexcess">Nexcess</a> or <a href="#kinsta">Kinsta</a> are much better choices.</span> 
<h3 class="shortcode-faq-question-inline">Which web hosts offer free SSL?</h3>
<span class="shortcode-faq-answer-inline">All hosts on <a href="#final-009" onclick="trackClickout('event', 'clickin', 'anchorLink', 'final009', this,  );">our top 10 list</a> currently offer free Lets Encrypt SSL certificates. Keep in mind that vendors sometimes change plan features, so during the sign-up process, be sure to double-check that an SSL certificate is indeed included in the package.</span> 
</div>
